{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:15:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:15:21","title":"How B2B Marketers Can Get the Most Out of Webinars in 2020","link":"https://www.toprankblog.com/?p=28792","description":"<p><img width=\"600\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/WebinarsIn2020ImageA600w.jpg\" class=\"attachment-post-thumbnail size-post-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"Businesspeople with Screens as Heads Image.\" srcset=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/WebinarsIn2020ImageA600w.jpg 600w, https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/WebinarsIn2020ImageA600w-300x180.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" /></p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28793\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/WebinarsIn2020ImageA600w.jpg\" alt=\"Businesspeople with Screens as Heads Image.\" width=\"600\" height=\"360\" />\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There has to be a word for the creeping dread B2B marketers have been feeling this year, preferably something German with a ton of umlauts.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As we watched events in the spring cancel, postpone, or go virtual, we held out hope that summer would be different. Then July’s events moved out. Now it’s looking like the type of large-scale events B2B marketers depend on will have to wait until 2021… at the earliest.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But we don’t have to despair! We can close the gap with virtual events. The speaking gig at an industry conference can become a webinar, as can a planned panel discussion or product demonstration. </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The good news is plenty of people have more spare time than before to watch your webinar.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The bad news is that everyone who </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">makes</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> webinars has time on their hands, too. So, your webinar has to have a little extra oomph to stand out in the crowd. </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here’s how you can level up your webinar creation and promotion.</span>\n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">How to Get the Most from Your B2B Webinar</span></h2>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s no longer enough to put up a slide deck and talk through bullet points. These tips will help you make a more compelling webinar — and make sure that people attend it.</span>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Start with Content Research</span></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">No marketer worth their salt would make a blog post without doing content research. Why should your webinar be different? </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To determine the best subject matter for your webinar, bring all of your research tools to bear:</span>\n<ul>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">SEO research via </span><a href=\"https://www.semrush.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">SEMRush</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and Google Analytics</span></li>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Question research via </span><a href=\"https://buzzsumo.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">BuzzSumo</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and </span><a href=\"https://answerthepublic.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">AnswerthePublic</span></a></li>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Prospect feedback from your sales team</span></li>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Competitor content evaluation</span></li>\n</ul>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">All of these resources will help you home in on the topics that your audience most wants to hear about. Your research might even drive what type of webinar you create: If your audience needs how-to advice, you might do a live demonstration. If they’re looking for thought leadership, you might partner with influencers. Speaking of the latter...</span>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Reach Out to Influencers</span></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In case you missed the headline yesterday, </span><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/b2b-influencer-marketing-2020/?utm_source=Social&#38;utm_medium=Lee%20Odden&#38;utm_campaign=2025%20State%20of%20Influencer%20Marketing%20Report\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">B2B Influencer Marketing</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> is kind of a big deal. There’s no greater boost to your credibility (and your potential audience) than adding industry thought leaders to your webinar. </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Look for people who are influential with your audience — those who are regularly producing content and engaging with anyone who posts a comment. They don’t have to have Taylor Swift-level follower counts to make a difference. They just have to be able to get a relevant audience’s attention and hold it.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Also, it’s not enough to just have someone appear with you on camera, though — it’s important to ask meaningful questions that will enable a substantive discussion. Keep your content research in mind as you plan the interview.</span>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Create a Landing Page &#38; Promote</span></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Give your audience plenty of time to prepare for your webinar. We recommend starting outreach at least two weeks beforehand, and up to a month if you can swing it. </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Create a short landing page to collect sign-ups — include a few key points you plan to cover, and introduce yourself and your guests. You can promote the landing page via social media — image-led social works well — and blog content that builds anticipation for your topic.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Don’t forget to include the webinar in your newsletter, and to enlist your influencers to drive pre-registration.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One great way to promote the webinar, and focus your content at the same time, is to poll your audience via social media. Ask for their thoughts on your topic. Ask what they most want to know about it. Ask what they would like to ask your thought leader guest. These posts can help drive registration while also making sure the content will be more relevant to the audience.</span>\n\n[bctt tweet=\"“One great way to promote the webinar, and focus your content at the same time, is to poll your audience via social media. Ask for their thoughts on your topic. Ask what they most want to know about it.” @NiteWrites\" username=\"toprank\"]\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Change Up the Format</span></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Q&#38;A, the panel discussion, the lecture — there are a few tried-and-true formats for webinars. But as the market gets flooded with content, we need to be more creative. For example, what about a working session instead of a discussion, where your panel collaboratively creates something? Or what about spicing up an interview with interstitial, pre-produced video content? </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You could even host the webinar on a platform like LinkedIn Live (while recording it for later publication, of course) and interact in real time with the audience. Just make sure to have a moderator to help keep the questions flowing smoothly.</span>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Plan and Practice, But Be Flexible</span></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s always a good idea to run through your entire webinar a few times before you go live. If you’re doing a lecture or presentation format, that means practicing all the content you plan to put across. For a panel discussion or interview, you may not be able to do a full run-through with your influencer, but you can still test the technology you will be using.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Don’t let your practicing and planning make your presentation too rigid, though. You should be able to follow an interesting conversational thread in your interview, or incorporate an audience comment in your presentation, without the whole thing going off the rails.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Of course, it’s always going to be tricky to run a live presentation, especially if you or your guests don’t do this type of presenting for a living. It can be challenging to think on your feet, come across as engaging, and keep a conversation focused and interesting to your audience.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Which is why I’m going to court controversy and say...</span>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You Don’t Have to Be Live</span></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As we think about changing up the format and offering a higher-quality experience to the audience, it may be time to let go of the idea that webinars have to be live. </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">After all, editing is the gift that you give to your audience. You wouldn’t write a blog post in real time with a hundred people watching. You wouldn’t record a podcast episode and publish the raw audio. So why not pre-record and edit your webinar?</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s true there is an immediacy to a live presentation that would be lost with a pre-recorded one. But the boost in quality for the audience could cover that loss. And you can still have an interactive experience with the audience through chat. You could even play the pre-recorded portion first, then hop on the video stream live for an audience Q&#38;A.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There’s an enormous gap between the standard slideshow &#38; lecture webinar and the produced, polished video that audiences appreciate most. Pre-recording and editing is one way to start closing that gap. </span>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Follow Up with Extra Content</span></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What should your audience do next after attending the webinar? That’s a question to answer before you take your first registration. Once you have a next step in mind, create a content bundle to send to each registrant after the webinar airs. This bundle could include a normally gated eBook or two, some recommended reading from your blog, or more content from your influencer guests.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You can also create extra content </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">from</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the webinar to help fill out your editorial calendar. Use excerpts from your discussion to fuel blog posts. Repurpose the audio as a podcast. Pull the best quotes to use as video posts on social media that drive to a gated version of the recorded webinar. Essentially, it’s about getting the most value possible from your content asset — the same thing you do with eBooks or blogs.</span>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Webinars Killed the Radio Star</span></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The pandemic has made webinars a go-to tactic for marketers who are missing out on face-to-face events. But as more marketers get into the webinar game, your content needs to be extraordinarily valuable and extremely well-promoted. If you plan, produce and promote your webinar with the same strategic care that you use for the rest of your content marketing, you’ll bring your audience more value and earn their attention in return.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Check out our CEO Lee Odden in a recent webinar: </span><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mM8yUidVf98\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Social Media in the Times of Social Distancing</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span><p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" 22:15:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:15:21","title":"Show Me The Numbers: 20 B2B Marketing Insights From Audience Poll Data","link":"https://www.toprankblog.com/?p=28881","description":"<p><img width=\"600\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/20PollDataInsightsImageA600w.jpg\" class=\"attachment-post-thumbnail size-post-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"Group of people with hands on a large colorful data chart image.\" srcset=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/20PollDataInsightsImageA600w.jpg 600w, https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/20PollDataInsightsImageA600w-300x180.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" /></p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28882\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/20PollDataInsightsImageA600w.jpg\" alt=\"Group of people with hands on a large colorful data chart image.\" width=\"600\" height=\"360\" />\n\nWhat can poll results tell B2B marketers about a year unlike any other, and how can this valuable audience data help us refine our marketing strategy as we push towards 2021?\n\nFor more than a year we’ve run weekly social media polls on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/toprank\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">our Twitter profile</a>, and for several months now have simultaneously also placed a weekly user poll on <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/company/toprank-online-marketing/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">our LinkedIn* page</a>.\n\nWe wanted to share some of the fascinating insights you have shared with us in the form of results from our polls, in order to see the trends that have emerged during this unprecedented year.\n\nLet’s look at trends in social media communications, how marketing is changing in 2020, and the rising effectiveness of <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/b2b-influencer-marketing-2020/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">B2B influencer marketing</a>, all through the lens of poll-derived feedback.\n<h2>Social Media Communication Expectations</h2>\n<h3>Insight #1 — Social Response Times</h3>\nHow quickly do we expect a response from a brand when we ask a question publicly on social media?\n\nThe majority marketers we polled expect to hear back from a brand within 24 hours, with 61 percent of respondents on LinkedIn expecting a reply within a day, 24 percent within one hour, and 16 percent by the end of the workday.\n\nTwitter respondents voiced similar sentiments, with 38 percent looking to get a reply from a brand within 24 hours, 33 percent by the end of the current workday, and 21 percent within an hour.\n\nIf you’re not answering social media inquiries within 24 hours you may come under fire, as not even one respondent to our poll said that they expect brands to take longer than a day to reply.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28883\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020July28LIPoll.png\" alt=\"2020July28LIPoll\" width=\"539\" height=\"375\" />\n<h3>Insight #2 — Email Response Times</h3>\nWe also asked the same question for a different form of online communications, curious about expectations when sending an old-fashioned email to a brand.\n\n50 percent of our Twitter poll respondents said that they expected an email reply within 24 hours, mostly echoing the expectations for public social media questions. 22 percent said they expected brands to reply by the end of the workday, 18 percent within a week — a notable difference from social media queries — and just 9 percent within an hour.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28886\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020February18TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020February18TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"360\" />\n<h3>Insight #3 — Unfollowing</h3>\nWhat drives people who have already taken the time and effort to follow a brand on social media to later unfollow them, and what messages can we learn from these mistakes?\n\nWhen we asked this question in a poll, our LinkedIn respondents said the top reason they unfollow brands comes down to posting poor quality content, followed by irrelevant content and brands that post too much content. Just two percent of respondents said that they unfollow brands that don’t post enough content.\n\n44 percent of our Twitter respondents said that irrelevant content was their top reason for unfollowing a brand, followed by poor quality content at 33 percent, and too much content at 22 percent.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28887\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020July14LIPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020July14LIPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"343\" />\n<h3>Insight #4 — Stories Format</h3>\nWe also ran a poll asking how the ephemeral stories format would fare on LinkedIn if the platform were to make its test of the post type a permanent part of the service. 33 percent of respondents said that LinkedIn Stories would be a great addition to the platform, while 25 percent felt it would be a good match. 25 percent also said that it would be an unlikely match, and 16 percent noted that the stories format would be a poor match for LinkedIn.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28888\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020May19TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020May19TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"362\" />\n<h3>Insight #5 — Experiential Content</h3>\nWe were also curious how B2B marketers are using experiential content in 2020. 58 percent of our Twitter poll respondents said that they expected to incorporate experiential content very frequently into their marketing efforts during 2020, followed by 41 percent who planned to do so somewhat frequently.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28889\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020March3TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020March3TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"389\" />\n\nExperiential content is playing a greater role in B2B marketing efforts in 2020, which I looked at in “<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/01/what-b2b-marketers-need-to-know-about-experiential-content/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">What B2B Marketers Need to Know About Experiential Content,</a>” and our <a href=\"https://twitter.com/NickNelsonMN\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Nick Nelson</a> examined recently in \"<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/05/hitting-a-content-marketing-home-run-with-experiential/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">How to Hit a Marketing Home Run with Experiential Content</a>.\"\n<h3>Insight #6 — Chatbots &#38; Artificial Intelligence</h3>\nHow B2B marketers communicate is constantly shifting as new technologies become available and gain wider adoption. We asked our Twitter followers who use chatbots or other forms of messaging featuring artificial intelligence (AI) to chime in on how the technology has performed for them.\n\n49 percent of B2B marketers who responded said that chatbots and AI-assisted technology has performed better than expected, yet 42 percent noted that the technology has under-performed, while 14 percent found that it performed as they had expected.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28890\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020May5TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020May5TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"332\" />\n<h3>Insight #7 — Virtual Meeting Length</h3>\nWe were curious what our audience of B2B marketers on Twitter felt the most effective length of time might be when it comes to virtual meetings.\n\n58 percent of respondents said that 30 minutes was the optimal length of time for effective virtual meetings, while 17 percent felt that 15 minutes or less works best, with 17 percent also noting that 45 minutes is the most effective, followed by just 5 percent who said an hour was best.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28891\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020March24TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020March24TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"386\" />\n<h3>Insight #8 — Reviews &#38; Testimonials</h3>\nAnother part of marketing communications is <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/04/b2b-testimonials-reviews/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">user feedback, reviews, and testimonials</a>, and we asked our Twitter followers to share how often they use positive reviews in their marketing efforts.\n\n47 percent of respondents said that they use positive reviews in their marketing efforts occasionally, however 23 percent noted that they never do, followed by 17 percent who said that they always do, and 11 percent who do so frequently.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28892\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020February25TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020February25TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"371\" />\n<h3>Insight #9 — Newsletter Preferences</h3>\nSpeaking of email, we also wondered when B2B marketers prefer to receive monthly newsletters. 45 percent of our respondents said they prefer the first of the month, followed by 27 percent who are fond of mid-month newsletters, 18 percent who prefer a time early in the month, and 9 percent who want to see newsletters arrive at the end of the month.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28893\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020February11TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020February11TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"393\" />\n<h3>Insight #10 — The Emoji Divide</h3>\nThe use of emojis in social media messaging was an area of contention among our poll respondents. 35 percent said that emoji were somewhat effective, while the same number noted their use to rarely be effective. 17 percent said emoji were extremely effective, and some 11 percent noted that they never use them.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28894\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020January28TwitterPoll500.png\" alt=\"2020January28TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"370\" />\n<h2>The Changing Face of 2020 Marketing</h2>\nThe global health crisis has changed the face of marketing events in 2020, as nearly all conferences have made the jump to virtual events, as I wrote about recently in \"<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/17-top-virtual-marketing-conferences-for-summer-2020-beyond/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">17+ Top Virtual Marketing Conferences for Summer 2020 &#38; Beyond</a>.\"\n<h3>Insight #11 — Virtual Event Attendance</h3>\nAre B2B marketers planning to attend newly-virtual events, and if so how many?\n\nWe asked our LinkedIn and Twitter users how many virtual marketing events they planned to attend over the final five months of 2020.\n\nMost respondents said that they will attend between one and five virtual marketing events, while the second most frequent choice was those who said they won’t be attending a single virtual event, followed by those who plan to attend between six and 10.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28895\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020July21LIPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020July21LIPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"339\" />\n\nVirtual events and webinars are undoubtedly seeing an unexpected golden age this year, and we’ve explored how to best utilize them, in “<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/b2b-webinars-2020/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">How B2B Marketers Can Get the Most Out of Webinars in 2020</a>.”\n\n[bctt tweet=\"“One great way to promote the webinar, and focus your content at the same time, is to poll your audience via social media. Ask for their thoughts on your topic. Ask what they most want to know about it.” @NiteWrites\" username=\"toprank\"]\n<h3>Insight #12 — Top Pain Points</h3>\nWe wanted to find out what the biggest pandemic pain points have been for B2B marketers, and among those answering our LinkedIn poll 64 percent said that a decrease in budget or business has been the top challenge, followed by the difficulty in engaging customers at 36 percent.\n\n46 percent of Twitter respondents also revealed that falling budgets and business were their top pain points, followed by engaging customers at 38 percent and remote work issues for some 15 percent of marketers.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28896\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020July7LIPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020July7LIPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"341\" />\n<h3>Insight #13 — Learning New Skills</h3>\n63 percent of poll respondents said that they have used their time during the pandemic to learn new marketing skills online, while 18 percent said that they planned to do so.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28897\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020May12TwitterPoll500.png\" alt=\"2020May12TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"356\" />\n<h3>Insight #14 — Digital Asset Management</h3>\n54 percent of B2B marketers we polled on Twitter said that they either already use a digital asset management (DAM) solution in their marketing stack or plan to implement one, while 45 percent didn’t use a DAM.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28898\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020April28TwitterPoll500.png\" alt=\"2020April28TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"311\" />\n\nIf you aren't familiar with how DAM can help B2B marketers, I looked into the issue in \"<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/04/digital-asset-management-tips-for-b2b-marketers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Why B2B Marketers Should Give a DAM: Top Tips on Digital Asset Management</a>.\"\n<h3>Insight #15 — Podcast Growth</h3>\nWith U.S. podcast listeners topping the 100 million mark for the first time in 2020, we wondered how the global health crisis has affected listening frequency among B2B marketers.\n\n40 percent of our Twitter respondents said that they have been listening to more podcasts during the pandemic, with 22 percent noting that they’ve listened to fewer, 18 percent about the same amount, and another 18 percent who said they don’t listen to podcasts.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28899\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020March31TwitterPoll500.png\" alt=\"2020March31TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"359\" />\n<h3>Insight #16 — Streaming Ad Use</h3>\nWith numerous studies showing that streaming music ads were booming in 2019, we wondered what B2B marketers planned for 2020, and 50 percent of our Twitter poll respondents said that they had no streaming ad plans for the year, while 25 percent said they planned to implement more streaming ads, 16 percent fewer of them, and 8 percent about the same.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28900\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020January14TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020January14TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"407\" />\n<h3>Insight #17 — The Customer Journey</h3>\nContent creation efforts are also shifting in 2020, and we asked B2B marketers to share which stage of the customer journey they are focusing on the most.\n\n47 percent of respondents said that generating awareness was where they were placing the greatest focus, followed by brand advocacy at 35 percent, consideration and intent at 11 percent, and evaluation and purchase at 5 percent.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28901\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020February4TwitterPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020February4TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"371\" />\n<h2>The Rising Effectiveness of Influencer Marketing</h2>\n<h3>Insight #18 — Influencer Marketing Program Length</h3>\nWe asked our LinkedIn and Twitter followers to chime in on the ideal length of time a <a href=\"https://www.toprankmarketing.com/services/influencer-marketing/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">B2B influencer marketing program</a> should run for maximum effectiveness, and the majority of our savvy followers chose always-on and ongoing programs — 73 percent of our LinkedIn respondents and 64 percent of our Twitter respondents.\n\nInfluencer marketing programs encompassing at least two campaigns was the second most popular choice, the choice of 21 percent of LinkedIn respondents and 18 percent of our Twitter respondents.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28902\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020June16LIPoll500w.png\" alt=\"2020June16LIPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"349\" />\n<h3>Insight #19 — Pandemic Focus Areas</h3>\nWe asked B2B marketers which area of marketing they were the most likely to increase focus on during the global health crisis, and topping the list was influencer marketing at 35 percent, followed by content marketing at 30 percent, search marketing at 20 percent, and email marketing, which garnered 12 percent of the poll responses.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28903\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020April21TwitterPoll500.png\" alt=\"2020April21TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"369\" />\n<h3>Insight #20 — Volume of Influencer Marketing Work</h3>\nWe were also curious how the pandemic has affected the volume of work B2B marketers have done with influencers. The greatest number of our respondents — some 36 percent — said that their volume of work with influencers had increased, followed by 32 percent who said that they didn’t use influencers, 24 percent who found that the volume of work was about the same, while 8 percent noted that the volume decreased.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28904\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/2020April14TwitterPoll500.png\" alt=\"2020April14TwitterPoll\" width=\"500\" height=\"368\" />\n<h2>Listening To Your Audience &#38; Taking Action</h2>\n<iframe class=\"giphy-embed\" src=\"https://giphy.com/embed/KyGno1zsRxg27aR31d\" width=\"480\" height=\"352\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe>\n\n<a href=\"https://giphy.com/gifs/KyGno1zsRxg27aR31d\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">via GIPHY</a>\n\nKeeping your finger on the pulse of your audience — whether it’s from poll results, surveys, questionnaires or other forms of feedback — goes a long way when it comes to making your marketing efforts authentic, and will help ensure that your communication is a two-way street and not just a publish-and-forget effort.\n\nWe hope you’ve found this glimpse into some of our own poll results helpful as you navigate the sometimes murky marketing waters 2020 has given us. Let us know your thoughts by voting in our current weekly poll about Instagram's new short-form video offering, Reels — you'll find it <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/feed/update/urn:li:activity:6698964421647171584/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">on LinkedIn here</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/toprank/status/1293198096936165376\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">on Twitter here</a>.\n\nYou can learn more about poll data and statistics, and how to get LinkedIn Polls</a></li>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2019/10/17-b2b-poll-insights/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">17 Revealing B2B Marketing Insights From Poll Data</a></li>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2018/07/power-social-media-polls/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Power of Social Media Polls: The Drill-Down on 3 eMarketingSEOBlog/~4/s8TKd-pwbfQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn80@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-15-25-083_f8f0c5b7f84f67a6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598278521881},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:15:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:15:21","title":"In Search of Trust: How Authentic Content Drives Customer Experience","link":"https://www.toprankblog.com/?p=28871","description":"<p><img width=\"600\" height=\"335\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/trust-authentic-content-cx.jpg\" class=\"attachment-post-thumbnail size-post-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"Authentic Content Customer Experience\" srcset=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/trust-authentic-content-cx.jpg 600w, https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/trust-authentic-content-cx-300x168.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" /></p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28872\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/trust-authentic-content-cx.jpg\" alt=\"Authentic Content Customer Experience\" width=\"600\" height=\"335\" />\n\nThe experience customers have through marketing content can be one of the most important differentiators for brands today.\n\nAnd yet 58% of B2B buyers don't not believe claims made by the vendors they most recently bought from (<a href=\"https://www.b2bmarketing.net/en/resources/news/almost-60-b2b-buyers-do-not-trust-vendors\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">TrustRadius</a>).\n\nIt’s hard to create a great experience if customers don’t trust brand communications.\n\nTrust is the gateway to influence perceptions, behaviors and actions and brands that want to succeed in the uncertain environment of today’s digital world need to double down on building trust with their customers. But how?\n\nToday’s increasingly digital buyers have high expectations of the companies they do business with: buyers want personalized and relevant information, they want a consistent experience across channels, they want confidence in the brand as a company that cares about privacy, their customers and the community.\n\nMeeting these expectations has been a challenge. From fake news to privacy issues to deep fakes, the digital world has become an uncertain source of information for consumers.\n\nTired of information overload, sales focused brand messaging and unremarkable content, 86% of customers say authenticity is important when deciding what brands they like and support (<a href=\"https://stackla.com/resources/reports/the-consumer-content-report-influence-in-the-digital-age/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Stackla - The Consumer Content Report: Influence in the Digital Age</a>).\n\nCustomers want what’s real. They want to trust and be confident about their decisions.\n\nWhile there’s a lot of information and even misinformation about content marketing and what it means for business communicators, there’s hope in building trust and influence by creating great customer experiences with authentic content.\n\nTo help marketers better understand how brands are winning customer hearts, minds, and trust with authentic content experiences here are 5 important steps:\n<h2>Accelerate Internal Credibility</h2>\nIn order for marketing to have the support it needs to be successful externally with customers, marketing needs to be credible inside the organization. Unfortunately, 80% of CEOs don’t trust marketers but 91% do trust CIOs and CFOs (<a href=\"https://www.fournaisegroup.com/CEOs-Do-Not-Trust-Marketers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Fournaise Group</a>).\n\nTo earn C-level trust, marketers must identify the key business problems faced by the business and make the connection to how marketing can help solve those issues. More importantly, marketing needs to provide clear direction about how and show credible reporting about impact. Ensuring credibility internally means promoting your wins to internal stakeholders. Make sure everyone from department heads to the C-suite are aware of the results that you are delivering to the business bottom line.\n\nAs marketers use content marketing integrated across channels to create “best answer” experiences for customers, marketers must also become the best answer for business growth inside the company by focusing on and communicating what matters to the business - not fluffy marketing promises with ambiguous correlations to the impact on the business.\n<h2>Double Down on Activating Customers</h2>\nWord of mouth and advocacy continue to represent important sources of trust and influence for brands. Marketers need to engage customers for reviews, ratings and even user generated content. As I’ve often said,\n<blockquote>\n<h2>“If you want your content to be great, ask your customers to participate.”</h2>\n</blockquote>\nBuild credibility and influence with customers by engaging them and making them part of the narrative that builds trust about your brand where buyers are looking.\n<h2>Work with External Influencers to Grow Brand Credibility</h2>\nEvery brand has a story to tell and to help make that story relevant, interesting and effective amongst buyers who are probably ignoring most brand communications, marketers can engage with relevant industry influencers. What makes someone influential is that they have the trust and attention of your customers. What better way to add credibility to your brand content than to collaborate with people who already have that credibility?\n\nVirtually any kind of external content that brands create can consider influencer collaboration to make it more credible, relevant, engaging and capable of actually reaching the audience it is intended for. Authenticity is essential for influencer collaborations to work so it’s important that marketers do their due diligence with influencers through proper identification, qualification and engagement best practices.\n<h2>Create a Content Collaboration Ecosystem</h2>\nMost marketers don’t have all the content creation resources they need to create the kind of content that drives customer experience. Engaging influencers to collaborate on content is a great start. But to truly build authenticity and content experiences that matter, customers can be engaged as well. User generated content is not for everyone, but when customers can contribute their voices to brand content, it adds a level of authenticity and trust that most marketing departments are able to on their own.\n\nEmployees are another important source of authentic content for brands, whether it’s telling stories about the impact those employees have on the lives of customers or by enlisting employees to help tell the brand story.\n<h2>Optimize Measurement to Customer ROI</h2>\nCreating trust with authentic content experiences must be a measurable exercise. Beyond share of voice and brand sentiment metrics, marketers must pay attention to measuring the effectiveness of content through the customer journey.\n\nAt a minimum, marketers must understand the the impact in these key areas:\n<ul>\n \t<li><strong>Attract</strong> - Is your marketing reaching the right audience in the channels they’re actually influenced by?</li>\n \t<li><strong>Engage</strong> - Is your marketing creating meaningful and satisfying experiences? Are you effectively using authenticity and influence to build trust?</li>\n \t<li><strong>Convert</strong> - Is the content you’re creating and co-creating actually inspiring action? Are those actions delivering impact for the business whether it’s brand perception, leads, sales or revenue?</li>\n</ul>\nBeyond these important steps towards more effective content marketing that drives trust are the influence traits brands must have to build trust:\n\n<strong>Purpose</strong>: “In this time of turmoil people are turning to brands as islands of stability.” Richard Edelman. How will the world be different after you’re successful doing what you do? How does that narrative translate into your marketing?\n\n<strong>Relevance</strong>: Use data to understand your internal/external customer and create compelling, useful content experiences that matter. Leverage the voices of your customers, prospects, and those they trust to help add credibility and context to your message.\n\n<strong>Reach:</strong>  Become “the best answer” for your customers with content that is easy to find and exists in context wherever buyers engage.\n\n<strong>Resonance:</strong>  Understand audience motivations through the buyer journey to inform messaging that “clicks” and inspires action and makes real, measurable business impact.\n\n<a href=\"https://summit.iabcmn.com/2020agenda/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28873\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/convergence-summit-2020.jpg\" alt=\"Convergence Summit 2020\" width=\"500\" height=\"263\" /></a>\nI hope you can join me at the virtual <a href=\"https://summit.iabcmn.com/2020agenda/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">IABC Minnesota Convergence Summit</a> conference this week where I will be giving the opening keynote on Wednesday August 12th at 4pm: <strong>In Search of Trust: How Authentic Content Drives Customer Experience</strong>. I’ll be digging into the current state of content marketing as well as sharing examples of brands walking the talk on authenticity and content marketing.<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/08/in-search-of-trust/\">In Search of Trust: How Authentic Content Drives Customer Experience</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" Odden","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/trust-authentic-content-cx.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn92@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-15-22-182_5c681d477013d5c3.webp","https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/convergence-summit-2020.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn87@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-15-25-219_c1c9a15114a73448.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/OnlineMarketingSEOBlog?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn11@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-15-22-140_b75958f276086430.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/OnlineMarketingSEOBlog/~4/YKOtS_CMKWY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn50@2020_1/2020/08/24/14-15-25-198_69c20cc0f23d7e97.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598278521882},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:15:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:15:21","title":"5 Tips For Finding Your Authentic Marketing Identity","link":"https://www.toprankblog.com/?p=28929","description":"<p><img width=\"600\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/AuthenticMarketingIdentityImageA600w.jpg\" class=\"attachment-post-thumbnail size-post-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"Collage of heroes and unsuccessful people.\" srcset=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/AuthenticMarketingIdentityImageA600w.jpg 600w, https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/AuthenticMarketingIdentityImageA600w-300x180.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" /></p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28930\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/AuthenticMarketingIdentityImageA600w.jpg\" alt=\"Collage of heroes and unsuccessful people.\" width=\"600\" height=\"360\" />\n\nWhat do you think of when you see a person’s business title, and how do the role assumptions we all inevitably bring to the table affect our ability to market authentically?\n\nCan we find our own more effective and authentic marketing identity and build greater business communication opportunities by ditching preconceived role beliefs?\n\nMarketing has seen dwindling levels of trust in recent years, and as our CEO <a href=\"https://twitter.com/leeodden\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Lee Odden</a> observed in his recent “<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/08/in-search-of-trust/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">In Search of Trust: How Authentic Content Drives Customer Experience</a>,” building great customer experiences is an uphill battle if customers don’t trust brand communications.\n\n<a href=\"https://stackla.com/resources/reports/the-consumer-content-report-influence-in-the-digital-age/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">86 percent</a> of customers have said that authenticity is important when deciding what brands they like and support, which ought to make marketing that resonates with truth a key goal among forward-thinking B2B marketers.\n\nUnderstanding that we’re not interacting with businesses but with human beings is also especially important as we push towards 2021, as our senior content strategist <a href=\"https://twitter.com/NickNelsonMN\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Nick Nelson</a> examined in “<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/03/how-authentic-content-builds-brand-trust-in-uncertain-times/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">How Authentic Content Builds Brand Trust in Uncertain Times</a>.”\n\nSo sit back and let’s explore how to find your most authentic marketing identity through the lens of authenticity when it comes to how we perceive the many professionals in our business lives.\n<h2>Looking Anew At Our Universe of Business Associates</h2>\nBack in 2011 during my decade as lead editor at search and social media conference Pubcon I created <a href=\"https://www.pubcon.com/dont-be-misunderstood-come-to-pubcon\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a grid image</a> in a style that was popular at the time, making light-hearted fun at how some people in the world of technology might mistakenly view those in different segments of the industry.\n\nIt highlighted how we sometimes tend to see ourselves and others who hold the same positions that we do in generally more favorable light than how we view our associates who have differing roles.\n\nBack then I included search engine optimizers, social media optimizers, social media marketers, chief executives, and affiliate marketers, and I thought it might be time for an update including chief marketing officers, chief information officers, and influencers.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28931\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/AuthenticMarketingGridImageA600w.jpg\" alt=\"Collage of heroes and unsuccessful people.\" width=\"600\" height=\"600\" />\n\nWhile “<i>To thine own self be true</i>” is unmistakably sound Shakespearian wisdom, it’s also important to see others as they truly are — without the prejudice of weighty titles.\n\nBeing true to ourselves starts when we strip away preconceived notions of what a CMO does or what a CEO doesn’t do and look instead at the totality of each person — a shift that can begin a newfound level of productive communication in both our professional and personal lives.\n\nAfter all, as <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/vanessacolella/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Vanessa Colella</a>, chief innovation officer at Citi, recently noted in an <a href=\"https://www.americanbanker.com/podcast/were-all-the-same-size-rectangle-on-the-zoom-screen\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">American Banker podcast</a>, “<b>We’re all the same size rectangle on the Zoom screen</b>.”\n<h2>Using A Fresh Understanding of Others To Learn More About Ourselves &#38; Tell More Authentic Marketing Stories</h2>\nWe’re all so much more than mere titles — each of us is a fantastic and unique collection of strengths, weaknesses, and the cumulative collection of professional and personal journeys our lives have given us.\n\nOur personal histories shape the stories we’re able to tell in our marketing, and making our storytelling authentic is a primary factor in making it successful.\n\n[bctt tweet=\"“We’re all so much more than mere titles — each of us is a fantastic and unique collection of strengths, weaknesses, and the cumulative collection of professional and personal journeys our lives have given us.” — Lane R. Ellis @lanerellis\" username=\"toprank\"]\n\nLet's now look at five tips for uncovering and putting your authentic marketing identity to work:\n<h2>1 — Bring Measurement to Authentic Content Experiences</h2>\n“Creating trust with authentic content experiences must be a measurable exercise,” Lee has urged. “Beyond share of voice and brand sentiment metrics, marketers must pay attention to measuring the effectiveness of content through the customer journey,” Lee added.\n\nIt's not enough to infuse authenticity in top-notch digital content, as to truly understand the significance and success of our efforts we need to incorporate a measurement to gauge performance.\n\nMeasurement comes in many forms, from manual to automated solutions, and each can only tell you so much if you don't have the proper key performance indicators (KPIs) relevant to your authentic campaigns. Albert Einstein offered insight that applies to marketing measurement and analytics, \"Not everything that can be counted counts, and not everything that counts can be counted.\"\n\n<iframe class=\"giphy-embed\" src=\"https://giphy.com/embed/3o6Ztfbym9laEgGpJ6\" width=\"480\" height=\"300\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe>\n\n<a href=\"https://giphy.com/gifs/einstein-albert-3o6Ztfbym9laEgGpJ6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">via GIPHY</a>\n\nWe've explored how marketers can measure for success in a number of articles, including these to get you up to speed:\n<ul>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/05/how-to-measure-marketing-goals-during-a-crisis/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">How to Measure Changing Marketing Goals During a Crisis</a></li>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2019/01/actionable-content-marketing-dashboard/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Measure for Success: 7 Secrets of Actionable Content Marketing Dashboards</a></li>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2018/12/top-analytics-advice-from-the-experts/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Measuring Content Marketing Success: Analytics Advice &#38; Insight from the Experts</a></li>\n</ul>\n[bctt tweet=\"“Authenticity is essential for influencer collaborations to work so it’s important that marketers do their due diligence with influencers through proper identification, qualification and engagement best practices.” @LeeOdden\" username=\"toprank\"]\n<h2>2 — Look to the Long-Term for Business Relationships</h2>\n“Content marketing is inherently a long game, focused on building relationships first and foremost,” Nick has observed. “Right now, the best way to pursue this goal is through authenticity and altruism, in the context of your business and its audience,” he added.\n\nAlways-on marketing has become more important in efforts to build trust, strengthen relationships, and achieve ongoing long-term success — a trend we’ve explored recently since the launch of our groundbreaking <a href=\"http://download.influencermarketingreport.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">2020 State of B2B Influencer Marketing report</a>.\n\n“As the need for B2B brands to reach and connect authentically with customers rises, B2B influencer marketers are evolving from transactional and intermittent campaigns to more relationship driven, Always-On Influencer engagement programs,” Lee observed in “<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/08/engine-influence-always-on/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">For Successful B2B Marketers The Engine of Influence is Always On #B2BIMReport</a>.”\n\nYou can learn more about how always-on marketing benefits B2B marketers in the following additional articles we've published on the subject:\n<ul>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/5-always-on-influencer-marketing/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Always On Influence: Costs Less and Better ROI – Here’s Why</a></li>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/06/influencer-relationships-crisis/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Always On Influence: Short Term vs. Long Term for Success During a Crisis</a></li>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/04/always-on-influence/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Always On Influence: Definition and Why B2B Brands Need it to Succeed</a></li>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/06/always-on-b2b-influencer-marketing-brand-research/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Always-On Influence: Why B2B Needs Brand Research</a></li>\n \t<li><a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/05/5-always-on-b2b-influencer-marketing-examples/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Always-On Influence: 5 Examples of Ongoing B2B Influencer Marketing In Action</a></li>\n</ul>\n[bctt tweet=\"“Marketers, brands, and creators of all kinds can make a positive difference. Being legitimately and authentically helpful in a moment like this can have a lasting impact.” @NickNelsonMN\" username=\"toprank\"]\n<h2>3 — Bring Authenticity to Every Facet of Your Life</h2>\nAuthenticity matters everywhere in our lives, and leading a life where we’re as authentic as possible in all areas makes it easier and more natural to incorporate it into our marketing efforts.\n\nUnforgettable marketing and <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/02/art-science-b2b-marketing-content/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">best-answer marketing</a> often go hand-in-hand, both filled with the kind of authenticity and genuine emotion that builds especially strong brand affinity.\n\n“Authenticity is a collection of choices that we have to make every day. It’s about the choice to show up and be real. The choice to be honest. The choice to let our true selves be seen,” author <a href=\"https://twitter.com/BreneBrown\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Brené Brown</a> has observed.\n\n[bctt tweet=\"“Building authenticity can be accomplished by sharing the kind of best-answer content that your audience is actively searching for.” — Lane R. Ellis @lanerellis\" username=\"toprank\"]\n<h2>4 — Purpose &#38; Authenticity Go Hand-in-Hand</h2>\n“Building a purpose-driven authentic brand brings growth,” Lee has observed, and during this year more than others brands have had to take a close look at their purpose and how they are pushing beyond words and into the realm of taking action.\n\nIn “<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/06/b2b-brands-take-a-stand/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">B2B Brands Take a Stand: 5 Examples of Going Beyond Words to Action</a>,” I examined at why it’s never been more important for brands to show purpose and to be connected to what’s important to customers, and seeing others and ourselves authentically can certainly go a long way in making this happen.\n\n[bctt tweet=\"“Don't mistake good communication for action. There is a really big difference.” Karen Kahn of @HP\" username=\"toprank\"]\n<h2>5 — Authenticity Builds Mutually Beneficial Programs</h2>\nIn <a href=\"https://www.toprankmarketing.com/services/influencer-marketing/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">B2B influencer marketing programs</a>, cooperative marketing efforts serve to benefit both brands and influencers, as <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dgingiss\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Dan Gingiss</a>, chief experience officer at The Experience Maker recently examined in our influencer marketing strategist <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dfriez\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Debbie Friez</a>’ “<a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/9-top-brand-marketing-tips-from-b2b-influencers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">B2B Influencer Marketing Advice from 9 Top B2B Influencers</a>.”\n\nWhether working with influencers or in more traditional marketing efforts, authenticity cuts to the heart of what drives the type of brand storytelling that truly connects with customers.\n\nIt's also the kind of authentic digital storytelling that is remembered well beyond the two seconds that recent research suggests is all marketers are likely to get these days — see \"<a href=\"https://www.thedrum.com/news/2020/08/13/you-get-2-seconds-engage-consumers-online-mars-neuroscientist-shares-key-findings\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">You get 2 seconds to engage consumers online: Mars neuroscientist shares key findings</a>.\"\n\n[bctt tweet=\"“The best influencer programs highlight an authentic relationship between the influencer and the brand, and the best way to accomplish that is to ensure a mutually beneficial program.” — Dan Ginigiss @dgingiss\" username=\"toprank\"]\n<h2>Authenticity Energizes Marketing &#38; Our Personal Journeys</h2>\n<iframe class=\"giphy-embed\" src=\"https://giphy.com/embed/lOUKVHqVTs7xBfv2Rk\" width=\"480\" height=\"359\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe>\n\n<a href=\"https://giphy.com/gifs/tcm-turner-classic-movies-metropolis-art-deco-lOUKVHqVTs7xBfv2Rk\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">via GIPHY</a>\n\nBeing authentic and true to ourselves is a process that can shift over time, requiring occasional reevaluation and possible adjustments to how we live and work. We hope these five tips for uncovering and putting your authentic marketing identity to work serve you well in your own personal journey.\n\nFinally, to further your insight into authenticity in B2B height=\"597\" />\n\nRecently we published the <a href=\"http://download.influencermarketingreport.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">2020 State of B2B Influencer Marketing report</a> after surveying hundreds of B2B marketers about their experiences, best practices, tools, budgets and plans for the future.\n\nIn an environment where B2B marketing is decidedly digital and marketers are hard pressed to squeeze more productivity out of fewer resources, credible information about marketing best practices, operations and trends for the future are in high demand. Judging by the response we've had to The State of B2B Influencer Marketing <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/b2b-influencer-marketing-2020/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Report</a> so far, we're definitely meeting a need.\n\nThere is both optimism and an unrealized opportunity with influencer marketing for B2B companies. For evidence, check out these stats from the report:\n<ul>\n \t<li><strong>78%</strong> of B2B marketers believe prospects rely on advice from influencers</li>\n \t<li><strong>74%</strong> believe that Influencer Marketing improves customer and prospect experiences</li>\n \t<li><strong>63%</strong> agree that marketing would have better results if it included an Influencer Marketing program</li>\n \t<li><strong>60%</strong> of marketers who use always on Influencer Marketing programs are very successful vs. 5% who do periodic campaigns</li>\n</ul>\nAnd yet:\n<ul>\n \t<li><strong>Only 19%</strong> of B2B marketers are running ongoing influencer marketing programs</li>\n \t<li><strong>Only half</strong> include a plan for influencer activation in their influencer marketing strategy</li>\n \t<li><strong>Only 35%</strong> of marketers use software to identify potential influencers</li>\n \t<li><strong>60%</strong> say they don’t have the knowledge to execute or have the right skills in house to implement ongoing Influencer Marketing programs</li>\n</ul>\nInfluencer Marketing is a significant opportunity for B2B Marketers to connect with <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/06/trust-marketing/\">trusted and credible experts</a> that have the attention of audiences that are probably overwhelmed with information and ignoring most of the ads that do get to them. At the same time B2B brands that build relationships to co-create content with these industry voices can integrate influence with <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/aoi-thought-leadership/\">thought leadership</a> to build the authority and influence of brand employees.\n\nIt is very satisfying to have spent the past 8 years focusing on such a niche aspect of B2B marketing to see it now start to grow in acceptance, adoption and maturity amongst some of the top B2B brands in the world.  Where there were previously no positions outside of PR with \"influencer\" in the title, now it is much more common to find marketers with titles like, Head of Global Influencer Marketing, VP Influencer Marketing and Communications, or B2B Influencer Engagement Strategist.\n\nMany B2B marketing professionals with these titles have earned hard won insights into what makes influencer marketing truly work for B2B, especially during a time when brand marketers are highly motivated to focus on strategies and tactics that will <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/06/b2b-marketing-pandemic/\">help them survive and thrive</a> during the pandemic.\n\nTo help you connect with the collective wisdom of the B2B influencer marketing crowd, here are 20 B2B Influencer Marketing Professionals to follow (in no particular order):\n\n<strong><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28818\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/Ursula-Ringham-SAP-1.jpg\" alt=\"Ursula Ringham\" width=\"200\" 22:15:21","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:15:21","title":"Boosting and Deepening Engagement through Empathy in B2B Marketing","link":"https://www.toprankblog.com/?p=28804","description":"<p><img width=\"600\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/BoostingEngagementWithEmpathyImageA600w.jpg\" class=\"attachment-post-thumbnail size-post-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"Business Professional Taking Notes Intently\" srcset=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/BoostingEngagementWithEmpathyImageA600w.jpg 600w, https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/BoostingEngagementWithEmpathyImageA600w-300x180.jpg 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" /></p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28805\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/BoostingEngagementWithEmpathyImageA600w.jpg\" alt=\"Business Professional Taking Notes Intently\" width=\"600\" height=\"360\" />\n\nEmpathy is more than a buzzword. It’s not a box to be checked, or an added finishing touch for content. If B2B marketers want to successfully engage human audiences and break free from the deluge of irrelevant messages swirling around today’s customers, empathy needs to be at the center of all strategic initiatives from start to finish.\n<h2>What Does Empathy Mean in B2B Marketing?</h2>\nEmpathy is defined simply as the ability to understand and share the feelings of another. But I’m not sure that characterization fully does it justice in the context of modern marketing.\n\nI rather like the way Zen Media CEO <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Shama\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Shama Hyder</a> described empathy in the <a href=\"https://monday.com/lp/better-creative-teamwork-expert-advice\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">better creative teamwork guide</a> we helped our clients at monday.com put together:\n\n<i>“Empathy is critical. It's much more than just having an understanding of what someone else's challenges might be. Part of it is that you have to give up being a control freak. As leaders, we should really look at the big picture and ask ourselves, is this necessary? Or is this just politicking, or someone trying to make it seem like it has to be done this way because it's the way they prefer?”</i>\n\nShama was speaking from the perspective of a business leader trying to get on the same page as their team, but it applies just as well to marketing endeavors. The critical first step in developing empathy is <i>disconnecting from our own ingrained perceptions and assumptions</i>. Only then can we truly understand and support the audiences we want to reach.\n\nToo often, empathy in marketing tends to be a bit narrow and self-centered (which is contradictory to the very concept itself). We often seek to understand only the challenges and pain points that drive interest in what we’re selling. Looking beyond this scope is necessary to build strong relationships founded on trust, especially now.\n\n“What you are creating, marketing and ultimately selling is but one piece of your customer’s life as a human on Earth. One very small piece,” said <a href=\"https://twitter.com/MaryBeech1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Mary Beech</a>, principal at MRB Brand Consulting and former CMO of Kate Spade, in an <a href=\"https://www.ama.org/marketing-news/how-does-empathetic-marketing-make-you-feel/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">AMA article on empathy in marketing</a>. “And if we aren’t keeping in mind their full journey, including their emotional, mental, social and physical needs — as well as the challenges and joys they are facing — we cannot do our jobs well.”\n\nAs <a href=\"https://twitter.com/briansolis\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Brian Solis</a> wrote at Forbes recently, the <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/briansolis/2020/07/09/in-an-era-of-covid-19-disruption-brands-must-rethink-marketing-as-empathetic-customer-experiences/#186775907aa1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">need for empathetic customer experiences is greater than ever</a> in the age of COVID-19 disruption. People have so much going on in their lives, and are facing so many unprecedented difficulties, that a myopic brand-centric focus is all the more untenable. “Traditional marketing will no longer have the same effect moving forward,” he argues. “If anything, it will negatively affect customer relationships rather than enhance them.”\n\nAgreed. So, let’s find a better way.\n<h2>Engaging with True Empathy in the New Era of Marketing</h2>\nImagine if it was possible to sit down and have an in-depth conversation with each one of your customers and potential customers. You’d gain first-hand insight into their worldviews, their challenges, their hopes and dreams.\n\nSadly, it’s not possible. You don’t have the time, nor do your customers. (Although I do recommend making a habit of engaging in direct, candid conversations with them when possible.) To make empathy scalable, marketers need to take advantage of all the tools at their disposal. This largely requires <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2017/12/data-customer-experience/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">using data to connect the dots</a>.\n\n“It’s critical for marketers to have a real-time 360 view and understanding of a customer’s full journey, at every stage, from discovery to engagement to retention and loyalty to advocacy,” Solis wrote at Forbes.\n\nHere are some suggestions for obtaining such a view:\n\n<b>Use empathy-mapping. </b>This practice, explained in a <a href=\"https://www.nngroup.com/articles/empathy-mapping/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">helpful primer from Nielsen Norman Group</a>, involves creating a visualization of attitudes and behaviors to guide decision-making. Empathy-mapping originated in the world of UX design, but given how much user experience and customer experience now overlap, it’s becoming a powerful tool for marketers.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28806\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/EmpathyMap600w.png\" alt=\"Empathy Map\" width=\"570\" height=\"602\" />\n<p style=\"text-align: left;\">(Source: <a href=\"https://www.nngroup.com/articles/empathy-mapping/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Nielsen Norman Group</a>)</p>\n<b>Coordinate and integrate your organizational efforts.</b> Every customer-facing function in a company — marketing, sales, customer service — sees the customer from a different perspective. Seek ways to bring all these perspectives together into one centralized, holistic view. Per Solis: “Cross-functional collaboration is a mandate. As such, integration will become the new standard and will quickly become table stakes as every company rushes in this direction.”\n\n<b>Tap into meaningful influencer relationships.</b> Influencers can play a key role in empathetic marketing because they have relationships and perspectives extending beyond our brand ecosystems. If they align with your audience, influencers can bring unique insight and connect at deeper levels. <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2018/12/influencer-marketing-mechanical-meaningful/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Turning influencer engagements from mechanical to meaningful</a> is essential to accomplishing this.\n\nIncidentally, Mr. Solis recently partnered with TopRank Marketing on the first-ever <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/b2b-influencer-marketing-2020\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">State of B2B Influencer Marketing</a> report, in which our friend Ann Handley summarizes the impact quite well: “You could call yourself a good parent or a world-class marketer or an empathetic friend ... but any of those things would carry more weight coming from your child, customer, or BFF. So it is with integrating influencer content: It's a direct line to building trust and customer confidence.”\n\n<b>Research and engage with topics that matter to your customers outside of their jobs.</b> Given the connotations of B2B, it’s all too easy to isolate our customer research around what they do professionally. But these are human beings with lives outside of work. To drive powerful engagement, marketers should search for the cross-sections between their brand’s purpose and values, and what matters to their customers.\n\nA good example of this is found in the <a href=\"https://www.ibm.com/blogs/think/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">IBM THINK Blog</a>, which is “dedicated to chronicling the fast-moving world of cognitive computing” and covers many important societal topics. (Recent focuses include a post on gender pronouns and a corporate environmental report.)\n<h2>Examples of Empathetic B2B Marketing</h2>\nWho’s getting it right and paving the way for a more empathy-driven approach to engaging B2B audiences? Here are a few examples:\n<ul>\n \t<li>My post on <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2018/12/b2b-brands-talking-consumers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">seven B2B brands that talk to consumers, not companies</a> highlights several instances of an authentic and relatable human tone shining through.</li>\n \t<li>It goes without saying that the video-conferencing service Zoom stumbled into a massive business opportunity with the dramatic pivot to remote work this year. The company could simply try to cash in and maximize that opportunity, but instead, they’re doubling down on building trust. Zoom’s CEO Eric S. Yuan recently wrote about his roots in China in <a href=\"https://support.zoom.us/hc/en-us/articles/360039993092-Zoom-s-Commitment-to-User-Support-Business-Continuity-During-the-Coronavirus-Outbreak\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">articulating his organization’s support for this embattled region of the world</a>, noting that Zoom is providing expanded features for free accounts and offering accessible resources and education. He also <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/alexkonrad/2020/03/13/zoom-video-coronavirus-eric-yuan-schools/#5be1772b4e71\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">made the company’s tools free to K-12 schools</a> (a potentially lucrative customer base) in March.</li>\n</ul>\nSeeing human faces brings an instantly relatable element to any B2B campaign. That’s why <a href=\"https://news.microsoft.com/stories/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Microsoft’s Story Labs microsite</a>, which frames some of the company’s initiatives and guiding principles around real people and their stories, is so effective.\n\n<img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-28807\" src=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/wp-content/uploads/MicrosoftStoryLabsImage600w.png\" alt=\"Microsoft Story Labs\" width=\"600\" height=\"372\" />\n<h2>Let Empathy Guide Your B2B Marketing Strategy</h2>\nIn order to walk in someone else’s shoes, you first need to untie and remove your own. Making empathy a core strategic pillar requires marketers to take a step back, disconnect from their ingrained perceptions and assumptions, and get fully in tune with the people they serve.\n\nOnly then can we create the type of relevant and personalized experiences that drive deep and long-lasting brand engagement.\n\nFor more tips that will help your business-oriented content strike notes of genuine empathy, read Josh Nite’s blog post on <a href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/02/humanize-b2b-content-marketing/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">5 Ways to Humanize B2B Marketing</a>.\n\n&#160;<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com/2020/07/boosting-and-deepening-engagement-through-empathy-in-b2b-marketing/\">Boosting and Deepening Engagement through Empathy in B2B Marketing</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.toprankblog.com\">Online Marketing Blog - TopRank®</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
